Hair cannot be too short; it shouldn't be too long either. With longer nails, you may be able to lift the edge of the wax easier. My hair was too long by the time I got the guts to try to do this myself. Stupidly, I didn't trim it. If you have too much hair/too long hair on the edge you're pulling from, it'll be harder to lift off the wax and get it going. This was actually the only case where I did hurt myself. Do smaller sections. It takes longer but it's easier. I started rushing, wanting to get done quicker by doing larger sections at a time, that's when I started to leave a lot of hair behind. I just don't have the experience for that yet. I didn't buy any numbing spray or any other prep or after products. I have to watch my $ and was able to do just fine with what this kit came with. But I was able to work with what I had anyway. Be careful, use common sense. Don't burn yourself. You want a nice thick layer of wax. If it's too runny, it's too hot and you may not be able to lay it on thick enough, even if you could tolerate the heat. As the wax cools, the surface will dull. When it's no longer sticky, it's ready to be taken off.If any wax residue is left behind, you may be able to lift it off by sticking the \\"not hairy\\" side of the wax patch to it and pulling it off.   81. I'm sooo glad I found this product on Amazon. I don't know how I was managing before I started using this. Just a warning: It does take a lot of practice, reading up on tips, and knowledge on how to use it before you are 100% comfortable and can do it quickly. However after you master it, it makes life so much easier, and it's wonderful. It saves a lot of $ in the long run. Reading all the reviews on Amazon helped a lot and it probably took me 8-10 different tries to really get the hang of it. It helps to even get the services done professionally a few times to get the idea of the technique. A few tips: -Heat it on high for about 10-15 minutes, just so the edges are melted, then turn it to low -After about 5 more minutes on low you can start using the edges or flip the hard center around so everything melts faster -Then throughout the whole process, I'm switching it back n forth between OFF and low to keep the wax consistently thick and gooey -You want the wax to be thick and gooey or it'll be a big mess of dripping wax everywhere -Use the pre-waxing oil they give you. It helps the wax from sticking to you. I made the mistake of copying what the salons use and used baby powder. It made a big mess and had residual wax stuck everywhere. Very hard to remove!! -Apply wax going in the direction of the hair and rip going the opposite direction -Make sure you apply the wax in thick /small strips, then after waiting 10 seconds, flick the edge up so you have a tab to pull from -After the ripping, use your hand to press down on the surface of the skin, helps the pain go away immediately. Sometimes I'll even rip an inch, press down, rip a little more if I can't bear the pain in one big motion. -When you run out, just buy re-fills, and make sure it's the hard wax. It makes all the difference!!

  91. This GiGi Brazilian wax kit really does have almost everything you need to do a successful Brazilian on your own. To start with what it comes with: GiGi Brazilian Hard Wax (this is the same stuff they use at the salon) GiGi wood sticks for spreading wax (when these run out, I'll just by popsicle sticks) Gigi Pre-epilation oil Gigi Post-wax cooling gel (this is *not* a wax remover) Gigi Wax Warmer (the true value of the kit, comes with a warmer, plastic cover, and paper ring to put around the wax container so it doesn't drip onto the warmer) Instructional DVD (meant for professionals and not super helpful to me) I have gotten Brazilians in salons several times before and I can't speak enough to the benefits of hard wax over strip wax for that \\"area.\\" Hard wax adheres to the hair, not the skin, so hurts MUCH less when pulling out (which is not to say it doesn't hurt, you're still pulling the hair out by the root). I once did a Brazilian to myself with those no-heat strip wax sets you can get at Walmart - OUCH. This is definitely better. I don't find the contortion too difficult - I put a towel down on my bed, lie down, put my knees up and do it that way. Definitely use the pre-epilation oil which will ready your skin for the wax. The warmer does keep the wax at a good temperature - you set it to high at first and when the wax melts, move the setting to low. Once the wax melts, apply SMALL strips and make sure the wax is THICK -- this make it easier to remove. Also make sure you've trimmed the hair and make sure you work so that where you're pulling from (the \\"edge\\" so to speak) is relatively hair free. I found that if I tried to pull from an area where the wax was already sticking to hair (as opposed to bare skin), it would be much harder to get out and ended up breaking a lot of the hairs, rather than pulling them out. It's tough finding that perfect instant where the wax has cooled enough to pull off quickly and with little pain, but I did it a coupletimes, and I'm sure I'll get better at it. I tapped the wax with my finger until it was no longer sticky, counted to ten after than, and then pulled. You can get pretty much all the hair this way but it takes a little while - I may get faster once I've gotten the hang of this stuff. The post-wax cooling gel actually burnt a bit, but afterwards I didn't have any redness or soreness. I wish Gigi included the Wax Off wax remover in this kit because that would have been really helpful -- you have to sort of pick the wax off if it cools too much, and wax remover would make things easier. Overall, a great kit, they really do use it in salons (when I went in to get my eyebrows done, I checked!) and it works well. I definitely recommend it.

  100. Like many other reviewers, my bottle of pre-epilation oil came open in transit. You would think they would shrink-wrap the bottles to prevent this, or at LEAST tape the bottle shut before shipping. On to the kit. This is an amazing value if you are brave enough to wax yourself. I have used it twice and the results were way better the second time, so I have faith that I will get better with practice. I put towels down on the floor and lie down. I have a lighted cosmetic mirror on a stand that I use to make sure I'm applying the wax correctly. It hurts much less if I lie down and don't look at the strip being pulled off. I think it's because I pull more quickly if I'm not looking at it. Here are my tips for success. If you have never been waxed before, I strongly recommend that you get waxed by a professional at least once before you try it on your own. This way, you can observe the professional's proper technique and hopefully emulate it on your own later. 1. Watch the instructional DVD. Note that the DVD is a professional video designed for estheticians, but it is NOT suitable for children. 2. Make sure the room is a comfortable temperature. If you get too hot and start sweating, the waxing results won't be as good. 3. TRIM hair to be waxed so it is between 1/4\\" and 1/2\\". If it is too short, the wax will be unable to pull out the hairs, and if it's too long, the wax will get stuck and it will be painful and dang near impossible to remove the wax. :( This is a major sadface, trust me. 4. Rub the pre-epilation oil in an area to be waxed, dab with a paper towel, then apply some baby powder. Dust off the extra baby powder if needed. 5. Don't let the wax become too hot. To start, put the heater on high for 15 minutes, then turn it down and keep it on the Low setting until it's ready to use. If you can scoop out wax with your wooden stick and spread it, you can start waxing. If it's too hot, it becomes very thin, and not only do you run the risk of burning yourself but you will also splatter wax everywhere. 6. Use small wax strips. Yes it takes a little longer, but they hurt far less. Also make sure the \\"tail\\" or end of the wax strip lands on an area without a lot of hair. This makes pulling the strip FAR easier. 7. After waxing, use the post-waxing gel, then LET YOUR SKIN REST FOR 24 HOURS. I refuse to use products with menthol so instead of the post-waxing gel, I use Paula's Choice Redness Relief treatment, [...] Once you have allowed your skin to heal, gently exfoliate each day in the shower to prevent ingrowns (I use a sisal washcloth, but you can use a gentle scrub, loofah, what have you). At least 24 hours after waxing, I use Paula's Choice excellent BHA/beta hydroxy acid lotion to help exfoliate the pores to prevent ingrown hairs and bumps.

Too much, and the wax will ball up and not stick. Too little (or you forget!) and you'll either bleed or break blood vessles under the skin. Rub the oil on like your applying suntan lotion. Just a fine layer. That's all! Key points to remember: -peel a little edge of the wax strip up from the bottom with your fingernail (if wax sticks under your fingernail, its not dry enough yet), use it as a tab, hold this tab as close to the skin as possible, pull the skin taught around the area with the other hand, and rip the strip quickly in the opposite direction of hair growth (don't rip upwards, rip backwards) Drink a glass of wine before hand too!
